<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Muscle_weakness" title="Muscle weakness">Muscle weakness</a> or <a href="/wiki/Lethargy" title="Lethargy">Lethargy</a>.</div>

<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Medical condition</div><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above" style="background:#ccc">Fatigue</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Other names</th><td class="infobox-data">Exhaustion, weariness, tiredness, lethargy, listlessness</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Medical_specialty" title="Medical specialty">Specialty</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Internal_medicine" title="Internal medicine">Internal medicine</a> and most other specialities</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Treatment</th><td class="infobox-data">Avoid known stressors, avoid unhealthy habits such as: drug use, <a href="/wiki/Drunkeness" class="mw-redirect" title="Drunkeness">excessive alcohol consumption</a>, smoking; healthy diet, exercise regularly, <a href="/wiki/Medication" title="Medication">medication</a>, staying hydrated, and <a href="/wiki/Vitamins" class="mw-redirect" title="Vitamins">vitamins</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Fatigue</b> describes a state of <b>tiredness</b> (which is not sleepiness) or <b>exhaustion</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-NHS_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHS-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In general usage, fatigue often follows prolonged physical or mental activity. When fatigue occurs independently of physical or mental exertion, or does not resolve after rest or sleep, it may have other causes, such as a medical condition.<sup id="cite_ref-ICD11_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICD11-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Fatigue (in a medical context) is complex and its cause is often unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-Nutrients_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nutrients-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Fatigue is associated with a wide variety of conditions including autoimmune disease, organ failure, chronic pain conditions, mood disorders, heart disease, infectious diseases, and post-infectious-disease states.<sup id="cite_ref-Finsterer_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Finsterer-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Fatigue (in the general usage sense of normal tiredness) can include both physical and mental fatigue. Physical fatigue results from <a href="/wiki/Muscle_fatigue" title="Muscle fatigue">muscle fatigue</a> brought about by intense <a href="/wiki/Physical_activity" title="Physical activity">physical activity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Mental fatigue results from prolonged periods of cognitive activity which impairs cognitive ability. Mental fatigue can manifest as <a href="/wiki/Somnolence" title="Somnolence">sleepiness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lethargy" title="Lethargy">lethargy</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Directed_attention_fatigue" title="Directed attention fatigue">directed attention fatigue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Marcora_2009_857–864_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marcora_2009_857–864-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Mental fatigue can also impair physical performance.<sup id="cite_ref-Martin_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martin-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definition"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Fatigue in a medical context is used to cover experiences of low energy that are not caused by normal life.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Distinguishing features of such fatigue include 
</p>
<ul><li>not linking fatigue to an obvious cause,</li>
<li>lack of improvement with rest,</li>
<li>variability in severity,</li>
<li>unpredictability, and</li>
<li>fatigue being more profound/overwhelming, and having extensive impact on daily living.<sup id="cite_ref-auto4_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Correlation of the quantum of fatigue with the severity of an underlying disease is often not present.<sup id="cite_ref-auto4_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Fatigue is multi-faceted and broadly defined, which makes understanding the cause of its manifestations especially difficult in conditions with diverse pathology including autoimmune diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2021 review proposed a definition for fatigue as a starting point for discussion: <i>“A multi-dimensional phenomenon in which the biophysiological, cognitive, motivational and emotional state of the body is affected resulting in significant impairment of the individual’s ability to function in their normal capacity”</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto4_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another definition is that fatigue is <i>"a significant subjective sensation of weariness, increasing sense of effort, mismatch between effort expended and actual performance, or exhaustion independent from medications, chronic pain, physical deconditioning, anaemia, respiratory dysfunction, depression, and sleep disorders."</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto9_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto9-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Terminology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The use of the term "fatigue" in medical contexts may carry inaccurate connotations from the more general usage of the same word. More accurate terminology may also be needed to cover variants within the umbrella term of fatigue.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comparison_with_other_terms">Comparison with other terms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Comparison with other terms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tiredness">Tiredness</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Tiredness"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Tiredness which is a normal result of <a href="/wiki/Work_(human_activity)" title="Work (human activity)">work</a>, mental <a href="/wiki/Stress_(medicine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stress (medicine)">stress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anxiety" title="Anxiety">anxiety</a>, overstimulation and understimulation, <a href="/wiki/Jet_lag" title="Jet lag">jet lag</a>, active <a href="/wiki/Recreation" title="Recreation">recreation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boredom" title="Boredom">boredom</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Sleep_deprivation" title="Sleep deprivation">lack of sleep</a> is not considered medical fatigue. This is the tiredness described in MeSH Descriptor Data.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sleepiness">Sleepiness</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sleepiness"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Fatigue is generally considered a longer-term condition than sleepiness (somnolence).<sup id="cite_ref-pmid16376590_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid16376590-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Although sleepiness can be a symptom of a medical condition, it usually results from lack of restful sleep, or lack of <a href="/wiki/Stimulation" title="Stimulation">stimulation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid4719486_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid4719486-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Fatigue is often described as an uncomfortable tiredness, whereas sleepiness can be comfortable and inviting.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Classification"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system_fatigue" title="Central nervous system fatigue">Central nervous system fatigue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muscle_fatigue" title="Muscle fatigue">Muscle fatigue</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_type">By type</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: By type"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Uni-_or_multi-dimensional">Uni- or multi-dimensional</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Uni- or multi-dimensional"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>It is disputed whether there are different dimensions of fatigue, such as peripheral (muscle) and central (mental) fatigue, or whether fatigue is a uni-dimensional phenomenon that influences different aspects of human life.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2021 review considered that different 'types/subsets' of fatigue may exist and that patients normally present with more than one such 'type/subset”. These different “types/subsets” of fatigue may be different dimensions of the same symptom, and the relative manifestations of each may depend on the relative contribution of different mechanisms. Inflammation may be the root causal mechanism in many cases.<sup id="cite_ref-auto4_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical">Physical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Physical"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Physical fatigue, or <a href="/wiki/Muscle_fatigue" title="Muscle fatigue">muscle fatigue</a>, is the temporary physical inability of muscles to perform optimally. The onset of muscle fatigue during physical activity is gradual, and depends upon an individual's level of physical fitness – other factors include <a href="/wiki/Sleep_deprivation" title="Sleep deprivation">sleep deprivation</a> and overall health.<sup id="cite_ref-WebMD_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WebMD-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Physical fatigue can be caused by a lack of energy in the muscle, by a decrease of the efficiency of the <a href="/wiki/Neuromuscular_junction" title="Neuromuscular junction">neuromuscular junction</a> or by a reduction of the drive originating from the <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a>, and can be reversed by rest.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The central component of fatigue is triggered by an increase of the level of <a href="/wiki/Serotonin" title="Serotonin">serotonin</a> in the central nervous system.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid10919962_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid10919962-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> During motor activity, serotonin released in synapses that contact <a href="/wiki/Motor_neuron" title="Motor neuron">motor neurons</a> promotes <a href="/wiki/Muscle_contraction" title="Muscle contraction">muscle contraction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> During high level of motor activity, the amount of serotonin released increases and a spillover occurs. Serotonin binds to extrasynaptic receptors located on the <a href="/wiki/Axonal_initial_segment" class="mw-redirect" title="Axonal initial segment">axonal initial segment</a> of motor neurons with the result that <a href="/wiki/Action_potential" title="Action potential">nerve impulse</a> initiation and thereby muscle contraction are inhibited.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Muscle strength testing can be used to determine the presence of a <a href="/wiki/Neuromuscular_disease" title="Neuromuscular disease">neuromuscular disease</a>, but cannot determine its cause. Additional testing, such as <a href="/wiki/Electromyography" title="Electromyography">electromyography</a>, can provide diagnostic information, but information gained from muscle strength testing alone is not enough to diagnose most neuromuscular disorders.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mental">Mental</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Mental"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Mental fatigue is a temporary inability to maintain optimal cognitive performance. The onset of mental fatigue during any cognitive activity is gradual, and depends upon an individual's cognitive ability, and also upon other factors, such as sleep deprivation and overall health.
</p><p>Mental fatigue has also been shown to decrease physical performance.<sup id="cite_ref-Marcora_2009_857–864_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marcora_2009_857–864-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> It can manifest as <a href="/wiki/Somnolence" title="Somnolence">somnolence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lethargy" title="Lethargy">lethargy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Directed_attention_fatigue" title="Directed attention fatigue">directed attention fatigue</a>, or disengagement. Research also suggests that mental fatigue is closely linked to the concept of <a href="/wiki/Ego_depletion" title="Ego depletion">ego depletion</a>, though the validity of the concept is disputed. For example, one pre-registered study of 686 participants found that after exerting mental effort, people are likely to disengage and become less interested in exerting further effort.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Decreased attention can also be described as a more or less decreased <a href="/wiki/Level_of_consciousness" class="mw-redirect" title="Level of consciousness">level of consciousness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In any case, this can be dangerous when performing tasks that require constant concentration, such as operating large vehicles. For instance, a person who is sufficiently somnolent may experience <a href="/wiki/Microsleep" title="Microsleep">microsleep</a>. However, objective cognitive testing can be used to differentiate the neurocognitive deficits of brain disease from those attributable to tiredness.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Perception" title="Perception">perception</a> of mental fatigue is believed to be modulated by the brain's <a href="/wiki/Reticular_activating_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Reticular activating system">reticular activating system</a> (RAS).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Fatigue impacts a driver's reaction time, awareness of hazards around them and their attention. Drowsy drivers are three times more likely to be involved in a car crash, and being awake over 20 hours is the equivalent of driving with a blood-alcohol concentration level of 0.08%.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Neurological_fatigue">Neurological fatigue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Neurological fatigue"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>People with <a href="/wiki/Multiple_sclerosis" title="Multiple sclerosis">multiple sclerosis</a> experience a form of overwhelming tiredness that can occur at any time of the day, for any duration, and that does not necessarily recur in a recognizable pattern for any given patient, referred to as "neurological fatigue", and often as "multiple sclerosis fatigue" or "lassitude".<sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>People with <a href="/wiki/Autoimmune_diseases" class="mw-redirect" title="Autoimmune diseases">autoimmune diseases</a> including inflammatory rheumatic diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Rheumatoid_arthritis" title="Rheumatoid arthritis">rheumatoid arthritis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psoriatic_arthritis" title="Psoriatic arthritis">psoriatic arthritis</a> and primary <a href="/wiki/Sj%C3%B6gren%27s_syndrome" class="mw-redirect" title="Sjögren&#39;s syndrome">Sjögren's syndrome</a>, experience similar fatigue.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto5_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto5-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_timescale">By timescale</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: By timescale"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Acute">Acute</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Acute"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Acute fatigue is that which is temporary and self-limited. Acute fatigue is most often caused by an <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">infection</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Common_cold" title="Common cold">common cold</a> and can be cognized as one part of the <a href="/wiki/Sickness_behavior" title="Sickness behavior">sickness behavior</a> response occurring when the <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune system</a> fights an <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">infection</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brain,_Behavior,_and_Immunity_2012_pp._552–558_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brain,_Behavior,_and_Immunity_2012_pp._552–558-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other common causes of acute fatigue include <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">depression</a> and chemical causes, such as <a href="/wiki/Dehydration" title="Dehydration">dehydration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poison" title="Poison">poisoning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Low_blood_sugar" class="mw-redirect" title="Low blood sugar">low blood sugar</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Mineral_(nutrient)" title="Mineral (nutrient)">mineral</a> or <a href="/wiki/Vitamin" title="Vitamin">vitamin</a> deficiencies.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Prolonged">Prolonged</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Prolonged"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Prolonged fatigue is a self-reported, persistent (constant) fatigue lasting at least one month.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources_(medicine)" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources (medicine)"><span title="Material near this tag needs references to reliable medical sources. (November 2021)">medical citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chronic">Chronic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Chronic"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Chronic fatigue is a self-reported fatigue lasting at least 6 consecutive months. Chronic fatigue may be either persistent or relapsing.<sup id="cite_ref-CDC1994_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDC1994-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Chronic fatigue is a symptom of many chronic illnesses and of <a href="/wiki/Idiopathic_chronic_fatigue" title="Idiopathic chronic fatigue">idiopathic chronic fatigue</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_effect">By effect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: By effect"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Fatigue can have significant negative impacts on quality of life.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Profound and debilitating fatigue is the most common complaint reported among individuals with autoimmune disease, such as systemic lupus erythematosus, multiple sclerosis, type 1 diabetes, celiac disease, chronic fatigue syndrome, and rheumatoid arthritis.<sup id="cite_ref-auto4_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The way that patients interpret and respond to their fatigue may also effect perceived impacts.<sup id="cite_ref-auto4_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Fatigue that dissociates by quantum with disease activity represents a large health economic burden and unmet need to patients and to society.<sup id="cite_ref-auto4_12-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Measurement">Measurement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Measurement"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Fatigue is currently measured by many different self-measurement surveys.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> There is no consensus on best practice,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> and the existing surveys do not capture the intermittent nature of some forms of fatigue.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> announced plans for a device to possibly quantitatively measure fatigue in 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> but the project was stopped in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Causes">Causes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Causes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Undiagnosed">Undiagnosed</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Undiagnosed"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The cause of fatigue is often undiagnosed.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Idiopathic_chronic_fatigue">Idiopathic chronic fatigue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Idiopathic chronic fatigue"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Idiopathic_chronic_fatigue" title="Idiopathic chronic fatigue">Idiopathic chronic fatigue</a></div><p> Idiopathic chronic fatigue is chronic fatigue not caused by a known proximate cause such as a discrete medical condition, drug or alcohol use.
</p><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medications">Medications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Medications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Fatigue may be a side effect of certain <a href="/wiki/Medication" title="Medication">medications</a> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Lithium_salt" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithium salt">lithium salts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ciprofloxacin" title="Ciprofloxacin">ciprofloxacin</a>); <a href="/wiki/Beta_blocker" title="Beta blocker">beta blockers</a>, which can induce <a href="/wiki/Exercise_intolerance" title="Exercise intolerance">exercise intolerance</a>; and many cancer treatments, particularly <a href="/wiki/Chemotherapy" title="Chemotherapy">chemotherapy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radiotherapy" class="mw-redirect" title="Radiotherapy">radiotherapy</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Drug_use">Drug use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Drug use"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Caffeine and alcohol can cause fatigue.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Obesity">Obesity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Obesity"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Obesity appears to correlate with greater fatigue incidence.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Psychological_stress_and_conditions">Psychological stress and conditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Psychological stress and conditions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Depression and adverse life events have been associated with fatigue.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Association_with_diseases">Association with diseases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Association with diseases"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Fatigue is often associated with diseases and conditions. Some major categories of conditions that often list fatigue as a symptom include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Autoimmune_disease" title="Autoimmune disease">Autoimmune diseases</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Zielinski_2019_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zielinski_2019-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> such as <a href="/wiki/Celiac_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Celiac disease">celiac disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lupus" title="Lupus">lupus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Multiple_sclerosis" title="Multiple sclerosis">multiple sclerosis</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Myasthenia_gravis" title="Myasthenia gravis">myasthenia gravis</a>, <a href="/wiki/NMOSD" class="mw-redirect" title="NMOSD">NMOSD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sj%C3%B6gren%27s_syndrome" class="mw-redirect" title="Sjögren&#39;s syndrome">Sjögren's syndrome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spondyloarthropathy" title="Spondyloarthropathy">spondyloarthropathy</a> and <a href="/wiki/UCTD" class="mw-redirect" title="UCTD">UCTD</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> This population's primary concern is fatigue.<sup id="cite_ref-auto5_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto5-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anxiety_disorder" title="Anxiety disorder">Anxiety disorders</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Generalized_anxiety_disorder" title="Generalized anxiety disorder">generalized anxiety disorder</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources_(medicine)" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources (medicine)"><span title="Material near this tag needs references to reliable medical sources. (July 2023)">medical citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Blood_disorders" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood disorders">Blood disorders</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Anemia" title="Anemia">anemia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hemochromatosis" class="mw-redirect" title="Hemochromatosis">hemochromatosis</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources_(medicine)" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources (medicine)"><span title="Material near this tag needs references to reliable medical sources. (July 2023)">medical citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Traumatic_brain_injury" title="Traumatic brain injury">Brain injury</a><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">Cancer</a>, in which case it is called <a href="/wiki/Cancer_fatigue" class="mw-redirect" title="Cancer fatigue">cancer fatigue</a><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Covid-19" class="mw-redirect" title="Covid-19">Covid-19</a>; long Covid.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Substance_use_disorder" title="Substance use disorder">Substance use disorders</a> including <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_use_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcohol use disorder">alcohol use disorder</a><sup id="cite_ref-Avellaneda_Fernández-2009_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avellaneda_Fernández-2009-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">Depression</a> and other mental disorders that feature <a href="/wiki/Depression_(mood)" title="Depression (mood)">depressed mood</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources_(medicine)" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources (medicine)"><span title="Material near this tag needs references to reliable medical sources. (July 2023)">medical citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Developmental_disorder" title="Developmental disorder">Developmental disorders</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Autism_spectrum" title="Autism spectrum">autism spectrum disorder</a><sup id="cite_ref-Williams_Gotham_p._56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williams_Gotham_p.-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eating_disorder" title="Eating disorder">Eating disorders</a>, which can produce fatigue due to inadequate nutrition</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Endocrine_disease" title="Endocrine disease">Endocrine diseases</a> or metabolic disorders: <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus" class="mw-redirect" title="Diabetes mellitus">diabetes mellitus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hypothyroidism" title="Hypothyroidism">hypothyroidism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Addison%E2%80%99s_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Addison’s disease">Addison’s disease</a><sup id="cite_ref-Friedman_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Friedman-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fibromyalgia" title="Fibromyalgia">Fibromyalgia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gulf_War_syndrome" title="Gulf War syndrome">Gulf War syndrome</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heart_failure" title="Heart failure">Heart failure</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Inborn_error_of_metabolism" class="mw-redirect" title="Inborn error of metabolism">Inborn errors of metabolism</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Fructose_malabsorption" title="Fructose malabsorption">fructose malabsorption</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Infectious_diseases" class="mw-redirect" title="Infectious diseases">Infectious diseases</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Infectious_mononucleosis" title="Infectious mononucleosis">infectious mononucleosis</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a><sup id="cite_ref-Friedman_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Friedman-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Irritable_bowel_syndrome" title="Irritable bowel syndrome">Irritable bowel syndrome</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kidney_disease" title="Kidney disease">Kidney diseases</a> e.g. <a href="/wiki/Acute_renal_failure" class="mw-redirect" title="Acute renal failure">acute renal failure</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chronic_renal_failure" class="mw-redirect" title="Chronic renal failure">chronic renal failure</a><sup id="cite_ref-Friedman_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Friedman-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leukemia" title="Leukemia">Leukemia</a> or <a href="/wiki/Lymphoma" title="Lymphoma">lymphoma</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Liver_failure" title="Liver failure">Liver failure</a> or liver diseases e.g. <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis" title="Hepatitis">Hepatitis</a><sup id="cite_ref-Friedman_57-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Friedman-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lyme_disease" title="Lyme disease">Lyme disease</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Myalgic_encephalomyelitis_/_chronic_fatigue_syndrome" class="mw-redirect" title="Myalgic encephalomyelitis / chronic fatigue syndrome">Myalgic encephalomyelitis / chronic fatigue syndrome</a> (ME/CFS)<sup id="cite_ref-Avellaneda_Fernández-2009_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avellaneda_Fernández-2009-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neurological_disorder" title="Neurological disorder">Neurological disorders</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Narcolepsy" title="Narcolepsy">narcolepsy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Parkinson&#39;s disease">Parkinson's disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/Postural_Orthostatic_Tachycardia_Syndrome" class="mw-redirect" title="Postural Orthostatic Tachycardia Syndrome">Postural Orthostatic Tachycardia Syndrome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Post-concussion_syndrome" title="Post-concussion syndrome">post-concussion syndrome</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Physical_trauma" class="mw-redirect" title="Physical trauma">Physical trauma</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Pain" title="Pain">pain</a>-causing conditions, such as <a href="/wiki/Arthritis" title="Arthritis">arthritis</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sleep_deprivation" title="Sleep deprivation">Sleep deprivation</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sleep_disorder" title="Sleep disorder">sleep disorders</a>, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Sleep_apnea" title="Sleep apnea">sleep apnea</a><sup id="cite_ref-Friedman_57-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Friedman-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">Stroke</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thyroid_disease" title="Thyroid disease">Thyroid disease</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Hypothyroidism" title="Hypothyroidism">hypothyroidism</a></li></ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_vs._secondary">Primary vs. secondary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Primary vs. secondary"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In some areas it has been proposed that fatigue be separated into primary fatigue, caused directly by a disease process, and ordinary or secondary fatigue, caused by a range of causes including exertion and also secondary impacts on a person of having a disease (such as disrupted sleep).<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gerber_et_al_2019_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerber_et_al_2019-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The ICD definition of fatigue
<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> captures both types of fatigue; it includes fatigue that "occur[s] in the absence of... exertion... as a symptom of health conditions."
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mechanisms">Mechanisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Mechanisms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The mechanisms that cause fatigue are not well understood.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Several mechanisms may be in operation within a patient,<sup id="cite_ref-auto3_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> with the relative contribution of each mechanism differing over time.<sup id="cite_ref-auto4_12-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Inflammation">Inflammation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Inflammation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Inflammation distorts neural chemistry, brain function and functional connectivity across a broad range of brain networks,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> and has been linked to many types of fatigue.<sup id="cite_ref-Zielinski_2019_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zielinski_2019-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Findings implicate <a href="/wiki/Neuroinflammation" title="Neuroinflammation">neuroinflammation</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Etiology" title="Etiology">etiology</a> of fatigue in <a href="/wiki/Autoimmunity" title="Autoimmunity">autoimmune</a> and related disorders.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zielinski_2019_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zielinski_2019-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> 
Low-grade inflammation may cause an imbalance between energy availability and expenditure.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cytokines" class="mw-redirect" title="Cytokines">Cytokines</a> are small protein molecules that modulate immune responses and inflammation (as well as other functions) and may have causal roles in fatigue.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However the inflammation model may have difficulty in explaining the "unpredictability" and "variability" (i.e. appearing intermittently during the day, and not on all days) of the fatigue associated with inflammatory rheumatic diseases and autoimmune diseases (such as <a href="/wiki/Multiple_sclerosis" title="Multiple sclerosis">multiple sclerosis</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-auto_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Heat_shock_proteins">Heat shock proteins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Heat shock proteins"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A small 2016 study found that primary <a href="/wiki/Sj%C3%B6gren%E2%80%99s_syndrome" class="mw-redirect" title="Sjögren’s syndrome">Sjögren’s syndrome</a> patients with high fatigue, when compared with those with low fatigue, had significantly higher plasma concentrations of <a href="/wiki/Hsp90" title="Hsp90">HSP90α</a>, and a tendency to higher concentrations of HSP72.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reduced_brain_connectivity">Reduced brain connectivity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Reduced brain connectivity"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Fatigue has been correlated with reductions in structural and functional connectivity in the brain.<sup id="cite_ref-auto6_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto6-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> This has included in post-stroke,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> MS,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> NMOSD and MOG,<sup id="cite_ref-auto9_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto9-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and ME/CFS.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> This was also found for fatigue after brian injury,<sup id="cite_ref-auto7_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto7-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> including a significant linear correlation between self-reported fatigue and brain functional connectivity.<sup id="cite_ref-auto10_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto10-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>(Areas of the brain for which there is evidence of relation to fatigue are the thalamus and middle frontal cortex,<sup id="cite_ref-auto10_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto10-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> fronto-parietal and cingulo-opercular,<sup id="cite_ref-auto7_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto7-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>  and default mode network, salience network, and thalamocortical loop areas.<sup id="cite_ref-auto6_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto6-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>) 
</p><p>Fatigue has been defined above as a "subjective sensation".<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The reduced brain connection mechanism raises the potential that the changed perception of fatigue is a result of changes in perception of the body interior status, rather than actual changes in body interior status.<sup id="cite_ref-auto8_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto8-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Behavioural responses will then also play a role in how the person reacts to the changed perception of fatigue.<sup id="cite_ref-auto8_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto8-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Diagnosis">Diagnosis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Diagnosis"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Dark_circles_(cropped).png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Dark_circles_%28cropped%29.png/220px-Dark_circles_%28cropped%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="106" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7d/Dark_circles_%28cropped%29.png 1.5x" data-file-width="286" data-file-height="138" /></a><figcaption>Minor <a href="/wiki/Periorbital_dark_circles" title="Periorbital dark circles">dark circles</a>, in addition to a hint of <a href="/wiki/Eye_bags" class="mw-redirect" title="Eye bags">eye bags</a>, a combination which is suggestive of <a href="/wiki/Sleep_deprivation" title="Sleep deprivation">sleep deprivation</a> and/or mental fatigue</figcaption></figure>
<p>2023 best practice guidance stated
</p>
<ul><li>Fatigue prevalence is between 4.3% and 21.9%. Prevalence is higher in women than men.</li>
<li>In the primary care setting, a medical or psychiatric diagnosis is found in at least two-thirds of patients. The most common diagnoses, in descending order, are viral illness, upper respiratory infection, iron-deficiency anaemia, acute bronchitis, adverse effects of a medical agent in the proper dose, and depression or other mental disorder (such as panic disorder, and somatisation disorder).</li>
<li>The origin of fatigue may be central (brain-derived) or peripheral (usually a neuromuscular origin). It may be attributed to Physical illness, Psychological (e.g., psychiatric disorder), social (e.g., family problems), and physiological factors (e.g., old age), Occupational illness (e.g., workplace stress).</li>
<li>When unexplained, clinically evaluated chronic fatigue can be separated into chronic fatigue syndrome (also known as myalgic encephalomyelitis [ME]) and idiopathic chronic fatigue.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>A 2021 German study found that fatigue was the main or secondary reason for 10–20% of all consultations with a primary care physician.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2009 study concluded about 50% of people who have fatigue receive a diagnosis that could explain the fatigue after a year with the condition. In those people who have a possible diagnosis, musculoskeletal (19.4%) and psychological problems (16.5%) are the most common. Definitive physical conditions were only found in 8.2% of cases.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The overall goal in diagnosis is to identify and rule out any treatable conditions. This is done by considering 
</p>
<ul><li>the person's <a href="/wiki/Medical_history" title="Medical history">medical history</a>, any other symptoms present,</li>
<li>evaluation of the qualities of the fatigue itself. Identifiable patterns to the fatigue can include being more tired at certain times of day, whether fatigue increases throughout the day, and whether fatigue is reduced after taking a nap.</li>
<li>sleep patterns. These can be examined by enquiring about quality of sleep, the emotional state of the person, sleep pattern, and stress level. The amount of sleep, the hours that are set aside for sleep, and the number of times that a person awakens during the night are important. A <a href="/wiki/Sleep_study" title="Sleep study">sleep study</a> may be ordered to rule out a <a href="/wiki/Sleep_disorder" title="Sleep disorder">sleep disorder</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">depression</a> and other psychological conditions.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Substance_use_disorder" title="Substance use disorder">substance use disorders</a>, and use of caffeine and alcohol.</li>
<li>poor diet,</li>
<li>lack of <a href="/wiki/Physical_exercise" class="mw-redirect" title="Physical exercise">physical exercise</a> (which paradoxically increases fatigue).</li></ul>
<p>Further tests may include
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Blood_tests" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood tests">blood tests</a> to check for infection or <a href="/wiki/Anemia" title="Anemia">anemia</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Urinalysis" title="Urinalysis">urinalysis</a> to look for signs of <a href="/wiki/Liver_disease" title="Liver disease">liver disease</a> or <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus" class="mw-redirect" title="Diabetes mellitus">diabetes mellitus</a>,</li>
<li>other tests to check for <a href="/wiki/Kidney" title="Kidney">kidney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liver" title="Liver">liver</a> function, such as a <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_metabolic_panel" title="Comprehensive metabolic panel">comprehensive metabolic panel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Other tests may be chosen depending on the patient's social history, such as an <a href="/wiki/HIV_test" class="mw-redirect" title="HIV test">HIV test</a> or <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_test" title="Pregnancy test">pregnancy test</a>.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Treatment_and_Management">Treatment and Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Treatment and Management"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Management may include the following;
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Review_of_existing_medications">Review of existing medications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Review of existing medications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Medications may be evaluated for side effects that contribute to fatigue<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (November 2021)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and the interactions of medications are complex.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (November 2021)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lifestyle_changes">Lifestyle changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Lifestyle changes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Fatigue may be reduced by reducing obesity, caffeine and alcohol intake,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> pain and sleep disturbance, and by improving mental well-being.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto4_12-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medications_used_to_treat_fatigue">Medications used to treat fatigue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Medications used to treat fatigue"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The UK <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_for_Health_and_Care_Excellence" title="National Institute for Health and Care Excellence">NICE</a> recommends consideration of amantadine, modafinil and SSRIs for MS fatigue.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Psychostimulant" class="mw-redirect" title="Psychostimulant">Psychostimulants</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Methylphenidate" title="Methylphenidate">methylphenidate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amphetamine-type_stimulant" class="mw-redirect" title="Amphetamine-type stimulant">amphetamines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Modafinil" title="Modafinil">modafinil</a> have been used in the treatment of fatigue related to <a href="/wiki/Depression_(mood)" title="Depression (mood)">depression</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-pmid18425966_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid18425966-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pmid19281939_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid19281939-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pmid26906078_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid26906078-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pmid34144366_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid34144366-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Medical_illness" class="mw-redirect" title="Medical illness">medical illness</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Chronic_fatigue_syndrome" class="mw-redirect" title="Chronic fatigue syndrome">chronic fatigue syndrome</a><sup id="cite_ref-pmid20088743_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid20088743-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pmid18505357_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid18505357-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid19281939_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid19281939-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pmid8856815_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid8856815-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pmid20870637_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid20870637-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pmid21251796_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid21251796-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pmid24416225_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid24416225-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pmid25299141_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid25299141-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pmid25814977_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid25814977-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> They have also been used to counteract fatigue in <a href="/wiki/Sleep_loss" class="mw-redirect" title="Sleep loss">sleep loss</a><sup id="cite_ref-pmid16268386_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid16268386-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> and in <a href="/wiki/Aviation" title="Aviation">aviation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid33754977_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid33754977-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vagus_nerve_stimulation">Vagus nerve stimulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Vagus nerve stimulation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A small study showed possible efficacy of <a href="/wiki/Vagus_nerve_stimulation" title="Vagus nerve stimulation">vagus nerve stimulation</a> for fatigue reduction in <a href="/wiki/Sjogren%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Sjogren&#39;s">Sjogren's</a> patients.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_purposes_of_fatigue">Possible purposes of fatigue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Possible purposes of fatigue"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolutionary_purposes">Evolutionary purposes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Evolutionary purposes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It has been posited that fatigue had evolutionary benefits in making more of the body's resources available for healing processes, such as immune responses, and in limiting disease spread by tending to reduce social interactions.<sup id="cite_ref-auto3_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Body_resource_management_purposes">Body resource management purposes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Body resource management purposes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Fatigue has been posited as a bio-psycho-physiological state reflecting the body’s overall strategy in resource (energy) management. Fatigue may occur when the body wants to limit resource utilisation (“rationing”) in order to conserve energy for a particular need, including a threat. This need may be a current or future anticipated need.<sup id="cite_ref-auto4_12-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Remnant">Remnant</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fatigue&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Remnant"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Primary fatigue may be a <a href="/wiki/Human_vestigiality" title="Human vestigiality">remnant</a> left over from earlier functionality, as the <a href="/wiki/Appendix_(anatomy)" title="Appendix (anatomy)">human appendix</a> is often seen.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-49">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Fatigue is a common feature of the anti-nuclear antibody (ANA)-positive systemic autoimmune rheumatic diseases (SARDs), including systemic lupus erythematosus (SLE), Sjogren’s disease (SjD), systemic sclerosis (SSc), dermatomyositis, and mixed connective tissue disease."</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A 2015 US survey found that 98% of people with autoimmune diseases experienced fatigue, 89% said it was a “major issue”, 68% said “fatigue is anything but normal. It is profound and prevents [them] from doing the simplest everyday tasks.” and 59% said it was “probably the most debilitating symptom of having an AD.” <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://autoimmune.org/fatigue-survey-results-released/">https://autoimmune.org/fatigue-survey-results-released/</a></span>

<li id="cite_note-80"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-80">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Fatigue is <i>"a significant subjective sensation of weariness, increasing sense of effort, mismatch between effort expended and actual performance, or exhaustion independent from medications, chronic pain, physical deconditioning, anaemia, respiratory dysfunction, depression, and sleep disorders."</i>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://academic.oup.com/braincomms/article/5/3/fcad107/7103314">https://academic.oup.com/braincomms/article/5/3/fcad107/7103314</a></span>
</li>

</li>
